## Domain Knowledge
**Domain**: materials science (solid mechanics / thermomechanical constitutive modeling)
**Analysis**: With sigma as stress, epsilon as strain, and T as temperature, the task most naturally fits thermomechanical constitutive laws for solids (elasticity/plasticity/viscoelasticity) where stiffness, yield strength, and hardening/softening depend on temperature.

**Common formula structures** (built-in generic + LLM domain-specific):
- Arrhenius equation: k = c0 * exp(c1 / T) (chemical reaction rate dependence on temperature)
- Coulomb's / Newton's inverse-square law: F = c0 / r**2 (gravitational or electrostatic force)
- Stefan-Boltzmann law: P = c0 * T**4 (blackbody radiation power vs temperature)
- Beer-Lambert law: I = c0 * exp(c1 * x) (light intensity attenuation through a medium)
- Michaelis-Menten kinetics: v = c0 * S / (S + c1) (enzyme-catalyzed reaction saturation)
- Hill equation: y = c0 * x**c1 / (x**c1 + c2) (cooperative binding, sigmoidal dose-response)
- Kepler's third law: T**2 = c0 * a**3 (orbital period vs semi-major axis)
- Newton's law of cooling: T = c0 + c1 * exp(c2 * t) (exponential thermal relaxation)
- Clausius-Clapeyron relation: log(P) = c0 + c1 / T (vapor pressure vs temperature)
- Langmuir adsorption isotherm: theta = c0 * P / (1 + c1 * P) (surface adsorption equilibrium)
- Freundlich isotherm: q = c0 * C**c1 (empirical adsorption on heterogeneous surface)
- Stokes' drag: F = c0 * r * v (viscous drag force on a sphere in fluid)
- Logistic growth: N = c0 / (1 + c1 * exp(c2 * t)) (population dynamics with carrying capacity)
- Planck-Wien approximation: I = c0 * f**3 * exp(c1 * f / T) (thermal radiation spectrum)
- Hooke’s law (isothermal linear elasticity): sigma = c0 * epsilon (small strain, linear elastic regime)
- Temperature-dependent modulus (linear in T): sigma = (c0 + c1 * T) * epsilon (elastic stiffness varies approximately linearly with temperature)
- Temperature-dependent modulus (polynomial in T): sigma = (c0 + c1 * T + c2 * T**2) * epsilon (elastic stiffness with curved temperature dependence)
- Thermoelasticity with thermal strain offset: sigma = c0 * (epsilon - c1 * (T - c2)) (stress from mechanical strain after subtracting thermal expansion strain)
- Nonlinear elasticity (Landau-type): sigma = c0 * epsilon + c1 * epsilon**3 (rubber-like or large-strain elastic nonlinearity in a simple series expansion)
- Power-law hardening (Hollomon-type, temperature-independent): sigma = c0 * epsilon**c1 (plastic flow curve in monotonic loading, empirical hardening)
- Temperature-softened power-law hardening: sigma = (c0 + c1 * epsilon**c2) * exp(c3 * T) (flow stress with multiplicative temperature softening/stiffening factor)
- Johnson–Cook-like (strain term × thermal softening term, simplified without strain-rate): sigma = (c0 + c1 * epsilon**c2) * (1 - (c3 * T)**c4) (plastic hardening with bounded thermal softening over a temperature range)
- Hyperbolic-tangent transition for glassy/rubbery or phase-change-like behavior: sigma = (c0 + c1 * tanh(c2 * (T - c3))) * epsilon (smooth modulus transition around a characteristic temperature)
- Saturating stress vs strain (approach to a limit): sigma = c0 * (1 - exp(c1 * epsilon)) * exp(c2 * T) (stress approaches an asymptote with strain; temperature scales the level)
- Rational softening in temperature (bounded decrease): sigma = (c0 + c1 * epsilon**c2) / (1 + c3 * T) (empirical temperature softening that stays finite)
- WLF-type temperature shift embedded in modulus (polymer viscoelastic temperature sensitivity proxy): sigma = (c0 + c1 / (1 + c2 * (T - c3) / (T + c4))) * epsilon (captures strong, nonlinear temperature sensitivity near a reference temperature)

**Formula structure heuristic features**:
- Oscillation damping envelope → Exponential decay envelope f(x)*exp(-c*Abs(x)) for symmetric damped oscillation, Gaussian envelope f(x)*exp(-c*x**2) for localized wave packets
- Saturation/clipping effects → Rational fraction x/(1+x), tanh; for variables with alternating positive/negative in oscillatory systems, selectively apply Abs
- Growth/decay → Exponential growth exp(c*t), Logistic 1/(1+exp(-c*x)), power law x**c
- Threshold/activation behavior → Max(x-c, 0), piecewise functions
- Coupling/cross effects → Product terms between variables x*y, power-law coupling x**c1 * y**c2
- Small-strain elastic regime → sigma proportional to epsilon; deviations suggest nonlinear elasticity (odd powers like epsilon**3).
- Temperature-dependent stiffness → model as E(T)*epsilon, where E(T) is often low-order polynomial or a smooth transition (tanh) around a characteristic temperature.
- Thermal expansion effects → sigma depends on (epsilon - alpha*(T - T0)); a linear shift in epsilon by T often indicates constrained thermal strain.
- Plastic hardening under monotonic loading → sigma grows sublinearly/superlinearly with epsilon via power laws (epsilon**n) or additive offsets (c0 + c1*epsilon**n).
- Thermal softening of strength → multiplicative reduction factors in T such as (1 - (c*T)**m) or rational 1/(1 + c*T) to keep sigma bounded.
- Phase/transition-like behavior (e.g., glass transition, melting onset) → sigmoid-shaped E(T) or flow-stress changes, well captured by tanh(T - T0) forms.
- Asymptotic/limited stress with increasing strain (damage, alignment, saturation) → (1 - exp(c*epsilon)) or rational epsilon/(epsilon + c) patterns for saturation.
- Coupled strain–temperature effects → use multiplicative separability (f(epsilon)*g(T)) when temperature mainly rescales the stress level rather than changing the curve shape.

I need to determine which candidates can be made equivalent to the ground truth:

**GT: 90.776*epsilon² + 2.482*(T - 337.769)*log(epsilon + 1)**

Expanding: **90.776*epsilon² + 2.482*T*log(epsilon + 1) - 838.769*log(epsilon + 1)**

The key basis functions in GT are:
1. **epsilon²** (coefficient ~90.776)
2. **T*log(epsilon + 1)** (coefficient ~2.482)
3. **log(epsilon + 1)** (coefficient ~-838.769)

No linear epsilon term, no epsilon³, no exponentials, no rational functions in the GT.

Let me systematically check each candidate. I'll focus on whether each candidate can produce exactly these three basis functions and zero out everything else.

For a candidate to match, it must:
- Be able to produce epsilon² 
- Be able to produce T*log(epsilon+1)
- Be able to produce log(epsilon+1)
- All other terms must be eliminable (set to zero)

Let me go through each candidate:

**Candidate 1:** `T*c0*epsilon + c1*epsilon + c2 + c3*epsilon³ + c4*epsilon²*exp(T*c5) + c6/(T*c7+1) + c8*|epsilon|^c9/(T*c7+1)`
- Has T*epsilon (linear in T and epsilon) but GT needs T*log(epsilon+1). Cannot produce T*log(epsilon+1). 
- Setting c0=0 removes T dependence, but GT requires T dependence.
- If c5≠0, epsilon²*exp(T*c5) has exponential T dependence, not matching.
- The term c6/(T*c7+1) + c8*|epsilon|^c9/(T*c7+1) = (c6 + c8*|epsilon|^c9)/(T*c7+1) - this is rational in T, not T*log.
- Cannot match.
Candidate 1 verdict: [NO MATCH]

**Candidate 2:** `T*c0*epsilon + c1*epsilon + c2 + c3*epsilon³ + c4*|epsilon|² + c5*epsilon*exp(c6/T)*log(c7*|epsilon|+1)`
- With epsilon≥0: |epsilon|=epsilon, so c4*epsilon²
- The T-dependent term is c5*epsilon*exp(c6/T)*log(c7*epsilon+1)
- GT needs T*log(epsilon+1). But exp(c6/T) is not linear in T. Cannot match.
Candidate 2 verdict: [NO MATCH]

**Candidate 3:** `T*c0*epsilon + c1*epsilon + c2 + c3*epsilon³ + c4*|epsilon|^c5 + c6*log(c7*(c8*|epsilon|+1)^c9 + 1)`
- T dependence only through T*c0*epsilon. GT needs T*log(epsilon+1), not T*epsilon.
- Cannot match.
Candidate 3 verdict: [NO MATCH]

**Candidate 4:** `T*c0*epsilon + c1*epsilon + c2 + c3*epsilon³ + c4*|epsilon|^c5 + c6*epsilon^c7*exp(c8/T)*log(c9*|epsilon|+1)`
- T dependence: T*c0*epsilon and exp(c8/T)*... 
- Need T*log(epsilon+1). T*epsilon ≠ T*log(epsilon+1), and exp(c8/T) ≠ T.
- Cannot match.
Candidate 4 verdict: [NO MATCH]

**Candidate 5:** `T^c0*c1*exp(c2/T)*|epsilon|^c3 + c4*epsilon + c5*epsilon/(c6+epsilon) + c7 + c8*epsilon*exp(c9/T)`

**Candidate 6:** `T*c0*epsilon + c1*epsilon + c2 + c3*epsilon³ + c4*epsilon²*exp(T*c5) + c6*exp(T*c7)*log(c8*|epsilon|+1)`

- c6*exp(T*c7)*log(c8*|epsilon|+1): need this to equal a*T*log(epsilon+1) + b*log(epsilon+1)
- exp(T*c7) is exponential in T, not linear. Cannot equal (a*T + b).
